Tooth Injury Rulings: Arsh, Qisas, and Defects
Enumerates specific cases of tooth injury, quantifying arsh and conditions for qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fixed arsh for teeth, identify conditions for qisas, and determine compensation when teeth are defective.

Core Idea
A tooth has fixed arsh of 500 dirhams, but defects change both compensation and availability of qisas.

This lesson examines a collection of Hanafi rulings on tooth injuries. You'll learn the fixed monetary compensation (arsh) for teeth, when retaliation (qisas) is possible, and how tooth defects alter the legal outcome. Special cases like a child's tooth and multiple perpetrators are also covered.

Guided Path
1
Parse the fixed arsh amounts
Read the initial numbers: arsh per tooth is 500 dirhams for a man, 250 for a woman. Multiple teeth are multiplied proportionally.
This is a fixed amount set by the Shari'ah, not based on market value.
2
Identify the command and consent scenario
Note the case where one person orders another to pull a tooth, then disputes the tooth. The commander's word with oath determines liability; arsh is on the 'aqlah of the commanded.
This parallels the rule for amputation on command.
3
Distinguish deliberate injury and play
Two men playing fight: if one breaks the other's tooth deliberately, qisas applies with conditions. But if each consented to a certain level of play, there is no liability.
Consent can negate liability in mutual play.
4
Analyze the defective tooth cases
Study the blackened tooth scenario: first perpetrator owes full arsh (500), second who pulls the now-defective tooth owes hukumat 'adl. Then compare with cases where the victim's own tooth is defective.
A defective victim tooth blocks qisas; only equitable compensation is due.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on child's tooth
Abu Hanifa holds no liability if a child's tooth is pulled and the child dies before regrowth; Abu Yusuf says hukumat 'adl. This is a valid scholarly difference.
The practical consequence: whether any compensation is paid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عشر ألفاً، وإن كانت أسنانه ثلاثين فعليه خمسة عشر ألفاً، ولو كانت ثمانية وعشرين فعليه أربعة عشر ألفاً وفي السراجية في سن الرجل خمسمائة وفي سن المرأة نصف ذلك. وفي الفتاوى : أمره بنزع سنه ثم اختلفا فقال الآمر أمرتك بغير هذا فإنه قال : القول قول الآمر مع يمينه فإذا حلف فأرش السن على عاقله المأمور أو في ماله لا رواية في هذا. وفي المنتقى قالوا: وليس في نفس الآدمي شيء من الأعضاء ديته زائدة على دية النفس إلا الأسنان . رجلان قاما في اللعب ليتضاربا بالوكز يعني مسه درن (حابرل فركب أحدهما الآخر وكسر سنه فعلى الضارب القصاص ولكن بالشرائط التي قلنا لأن هذا عمد والمسئلة كانت واقعة الفتوى على هذا وفي الظهيرية ولو قال كل واحد منهما (درن) فوكز أحدهما صاحبه لا شيء عليه وهو الصحيح بمنزلة قوله اقطع يدي ،فقطعها، وإذا قلع سن صبي وآخر حولاً فمات الصبي قبل تمام الحول فلا شيء على الجاني في قول أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف : فيه حكومة عدل وفي الكبرى قال : فيه حكومة عدل، وإذا ضرب سن رجل فاسود سن الرجل ثم جاء آخر فنزعها فعلى الأول تمام أرشها. وفي الخانية : خمسمائة وعلى الثاني حكومة عدل، وإذا نزع سن رجل وسن الثاني سوداء أو صفراء أو حمراء أو خضراء والنزع كان عمداً يخير المجني عليه إن شاء اقتص منه، وإن شاء ضمنه أرش سنه خمسمائة . وإن كان المعيوب سن المجني عليه فله حكومة عدل ولا يقتص سنه لسنه . وفي الخانية : ولو ضرب سن إنسان فاسودت وسن الجاني سوداء أو حمراء أو خضراء أو صفراء كان المجني عليه بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه، وإن شاء استوفى القصاص ناقصاً. وفي الكبرى ولو نزع سن رجل فنبت نصفها فعليه نصف أرشها وإن نبتت صفراء ففيها حكومة عدل .
Ten thousand, and if his teeth were thirty then on him is fifteen thousand, and if they were twenty-eight then on him is fourteen thousand. In al-Sirajiyyah: For a man's tooth is five hundred, and for a woman's tooth is half of that. In al-Fatawa: He commanded him to pull out his tooth, then they disagreed; the commander said 'I commanded you with other than this'—so he said: The statement of the commander is accepted with his oath. If he swears, then the arsh of the tooth is on the 'aqlah (tribe) of the commanded or from his own wealth; no narration in this. In al-Muntaqa they said: There is not in the human being any organ whose diyah exceeds the diyah of the soul except the teeth. Two men stood in play to strike each other with fists (meaning...? unclear) one rode the other and broke his tooth—so on the striker is qisas, but with the conditions we mentioned because this is deliberate; and the issue was a fatwa on this. In al-Zahiriyyah: If each of them said '?', and one struck his companion, there is nothing on him; this is the correct view, analogous to his saying 'Cut my hand', so he cut it. And if one pulls out the tooth of a child and the child has a year to live, then the child dies before completing the year, then there is nothing on the perpetrator according to Abu Hanifah. Abu Yusuf said: There is hukumat 'adl. In al-Kubra he said: There is hukumat 'adl. If one strikes a man's tooth and it blackens, then another comes and pulls it out, then on the first is the full arsh of it. In al-Khaniyyah: Five hundred, and on the second is hukumat 'adl. If one pulls out a man's tooth and the tooth of the second is black or yellow or red or green, and the pulling was deliberate, the victim chooses: if he wishes he may retaliate, and if he wishes he may demand the arsh of his tooth, five hundred. If the defective tooth belongs to the victim, then he has hukumat 'adl, and he does not retaliate a tooth for his tooth. In al-Khaniyyah: If one strikes a person's tooth and it blackens, and the perpetrator's tooth is black or red or green or yellow, the victim has the choice: if he wishes he may demand compensation, and if he wishes he may take qisas deficiently. In al-Kubra: If one pulls out a man's tooth and half of it grows back, then on him is half its arsh; if it grows back yellow, then there is hukumat 'adl.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (furu') regarding tooth (sin) injuries and their legal consequences. The author presents specific amounts of arsh (monetary compensation) for teeth: for a man's tooth the full arsh is 500 dirhams, for a woman half that. If multiple teeth are involved, the arsh is proportional (e.g., 10 teeth = 10,000, 30 teeth = 15,000, etc.). The passage then discusses cases where a person commands another to pull out a tooth (amr bi-naz') — a dispute arises about whether the commanded tooth was the intended one; the commander's word is taken with his oath, and if he swears, the arsh is on the 'aqlah (tribe) of the commanded or on his own wealth. Another case: two men playing fight (la'b), one strikes and breaks the other's tooth—this is considered deliberate ('amd), so qisas applies if conditions are met. Also: if a man says something like 'cut my hand' and the other does so, there is no liability (analogous to voluntary consent). Regarding a child's tooth: if the child dies before the tooth would have grown back, Abu Hanifa holds no liability, while Abu Yusuf says there is hukumat 'adl (equitable compensation). A key case: if a tooth is struck and turns black, then another person pulls it out—the first perpetrator owes full arsh (500), the second owes hukumat 'adl because he removed a defective tooth. If the perpetrator's own tooth is defective (black, etc.), the victim may choose between qisas (even if deficient) or arsh. If the victim's tooth is defective, he only gets hukumat 'adl and no qisas. If a pulled tooth grows back partially, arsh is proportional (half if half grows back); if it grows back yellow, hukumat 'adl.

Key Terms
سن (sinn): Tooth; includes all teeth (incisors, molars) for purposes of legal retaliation and compensation.
أرش (arsh): Monetary compensation for injury to a body part, fixed by shari'ah (e.g., for tooth 500).
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): Equitable compensation assessed by a qualified expert, not fixed by shari'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does a person owe if he pulls out a healthy tooth that later turns black and then is pulled by another?
A) Both owe five hundred each.
B) The first owes full arsh (500), the second owes hukumat 'adl.
C) The first owes hukumat 'adl, the second owes full arsh.
D) Neither owes anything because the tooth was already damaged.

Key Takeaway
A tooth has a fixed arsh of 500 dirhams for a man, but defects change both the compensation type (arsh or hukumat 'adl) and the availability of qisas.

Compensation for Cutting Male Genitalia and Buttocks
Explains compensation for cutting male organs and buttocks, including sequential injuries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the compensation amounts for simultaneous and sequential cutting of the penis and testicles, and apply the rule of hukumat al-adl when appropriate.

Core Idea
Compensation for cutting male organs depends on order: simultaneous = two diyahs; sequential = first full diyah, second only hukumat if benefit already lost.

This lesson covers the levels of monetary compensation (diyah and hukumat al-adl) for cutting the penis, testicles, and buttocks under Hanafi law. The rulings differentiate between simultaneous and sequential injuries, reflecting the principle that compensation may be reduced when the function of a later-cut organ is already nullified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
Determine what body part is cut and whether the act is intentional or mistaken. The general hukm is that cutting these parts obligates compensation (wajib).
The level of compensation depends on the order of cuts.
2
Distinguish simultaneous vs sequential
If the penis and testicles are cut together in one blow, two full diyahs are due. If cut separately, the order matters.
3
Apply the sequential rule
If the penis is cut first, then testicles: two full diyahs (because cutting the penis already eliminated the testicles' benefit). If testicles are cut first, then penis: diyah for testicles and hukumat al-adl for penis (since its function was already lost).
Hukumat al-adl is arbitrated compensation for an injury without a fixed diyah.
4
Extend to buttocks
Cutting both buttocks by mistake incurs full diyah; cutting one incurs half diyah, as per al-Zahiriyya.
5
Consider special cases
If one testicle is cut and sperm production ceases, compensation is one and a half diyah, but only if the offender confesses to the loss of function.
Intentional cutting of testicles may require qisas (retaliation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع الذكر جملة واحدة في حالة واحدة يجب عليه ديتان : دية بإزاء الذكر ودية بإزاء الأنثيين. وإذا قطع الذكر أولاً ثم الأنثيين يجب ديتان أيضاً لأن بقطع الذكر قطع منفعة الأنثيين وهي إمساك المني، فأما إذا قطع الأنثيين أولاً ثم الذكر تجب الدية بقطع الأنثيين وتجب بقطع الذكر حكومة العدل، وفي الإليتين إذا قطعتا خطأ كمال الدية. وفي الظهيرية : وفي أحدهما نصف الدية. وفي المنتقى عن محمد : إذا قطع إحدى أنثييه وانقطع ماؤه دية ونصف قال: ولا نعلم ذهاب الماء إلا باقرار الجاني فإذا قطع الباقي من إحدى الأنثيين يجب نصف الدية. ولم يذكر في الكتاب الحكم في العمد والظاهر الأنثيين أنه يجب فيه القصاص حالة العمد
With the penis and testicles together in one instance, two blood moneys are obligatory: a blood money for the penis and a blood money for the testicles. If he cuts the penis first then the testicles, two blood moneys are also obligatory because by cutting the penis he cuts off the benefit of the testicles, which is retention of semen. But if he cuts the testicles first then the penis, the blood money is obligatory for cutting the testicles, and for cutting the penis hukumat al-adl is obligatory. Regarding the two buttocks, if they are cut by mistake, the full blood money is due. In al-Zahiriyya: in one of them half the blood money. In al-Muntaqa from Muhammad: if he cuts one of his testicles and his sperm ceases, a blood money and a half. He said: we do not know of cessation of water except by the confession of the offender. So if he cuts the remaining of one testicle, half the blood money is obligatory. He did not mention in the book the ruling in intentionality, and outwardly regarding the testicles, retaliation is obligatory in the case of intentionality.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rulings on injuries to the male genitals and buttocks. The author first states the rule for simultaneous cutting: two full diyahs, one for the penis and one for the testicles. Then he addresses sequential cutting: if the penis is cut first, the benefit of the testicles is already lost, so cutting them later still incurs a full diyah. However, if the testicles are cut first, the later cutting of the penis only warrants hukumat al-adl (arbitrated compensation) because the full penalty for the penis was already partially satisfied by the loss of its function. The buttocks rule is then given: accidental cutting of both requires full diyah; according to al-Zahiriyya, one buttock requires half diyah. A transmission from Muhammad al-Shaybani adds: if one testicle is cut and sperm production stops, the compensation is one and a half diyah (one for the testicle and half for the lost function). This only applies if the offender confesses; otherwise, the lost function cannot be assumed. Finally, the text notes that intentional cutting of the testicles requires retaliation, as per the general principle for intentional injury.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Fixed monetary compensation for bodily injury or homicide, as determined by sharia.
حكومة العدل (hukumat al-adl): Arbitrated compensation for an injury that has no fixed diyah, assessed by a just arbitrator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the two buttocks are cut accidentally, what is the compensation?
A) Full diyah
B) Half diyah
C) Hukumat al-adl
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school applies a nuanced approach to compensation for serial injuries, reducing the amount when the function of a later-cut part is already nullified.

Compensation and Retaliation for Lower Limb Injuries
Fixed compensations for lower limb injuries and the rule for healed fractures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah amounts for feet and toes, identify the condition for qisas (cut from joint), and distinguish Abu Hanifa's ruling from Abu Yusuf's on healed fractures.

Core Idea
No compensation for a bone that heals perfectly — compensation is only for lasting defect.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers fixed compensations (diyah) and retaliation for intentional/accidental injuries to the feet and toes, and the rule for bone fractures. It also explains an important analogy: accidental cutting of a leg from mid-calf is treated like an accidental cut of a hand from mid-forearm. A key intra-Hanafi dispute appears regarding whether a fracture that heals perfectly still requires compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the injury type and location
Determine if the injury is to a foot, toe, leg, or bone. Distinguish intentional vs. accidental. For fractures, note whether the bone has healed with or without defect.
The ruling depends on these factors.
2
Apply fixed diyah for accidental foot/toe injuries
For both feet accidentally: full diyah. One foot: half. Each toe: one-tenth of diyah (so ten toes = full diyah).
These are fixed amounts.
3
Check qisas condition for intentional cutting
For intentional amputation of a foot or toe, qisas is required only if the cut is at a joint (ankle, knee, hip, toe joint). If cut elsewhere, only diyah is due.
Qisas requires precise equivalence.
4
Apply the hand analogy for accidental mid-calf cuts
If a leg is accidentally cut from mid-calf, the victim receives full diyah for the foot (since the foot is lost) plus hukumat al-adl for the rest of the leg below the knee—just like a hand cut from mid-forearm.
This is qiyas: the asl is the hand case.
5
Evaluate fracture compensation: perfect healing vs. defect
Abu Hanifa: if a bone breaks and heals perfectly without defect, no compensation. If a defect (e.g., swelling) remains, proportional compensation. Abu Yusuf requires hukumat al-adl even for perfect healing.
Mufta bihi: Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الرجلين كمال الدية في الخطأ، وفي أحدهما نصف الدية، وفي كل أصبع من أصابع الرجلين عشر الدية، وفي الرجل في العمد القصاص إذا قطع من مفصل القدم أو من مفصل الركبة أو من مفصل الورك، وإن قطعت من غير المفصل لا يجب القصاص. وفي الذخيرة : وكذلك الحكم في أصابع الرجلين إن قطعت من المفصل عمداً يجب القصاص، وإذا قطع الرجل خطأ من نصف الساق تجب الدية لأجل القدم وحكومة العدل فيما وراء القدم والكلام فيه نظير الكلام في اليد إذا قطعت من نصف الساعد. وإن كسر فخذه فبرأت واستقامت فلا شيء عليه، وفي قول أبي يوسف حكومة عدل، وذكر أبو سليمان عن محمد في كتاب الخراج قال أبو حنيفة : ما انكسر من إنسان يداً أو رجلاً أو غير ذلك وبرىء وعاد كهيئته فليس فيه عقل، وإن كان فيه نقص بأن برىء العظم وبقي فيه ورم ففيه من عقله بحساب ما نقص، وكذلك في الجراحة الجسد إذا برأ وعاد كهيئة فليس فيه شيء.
Regarding the two feet, the full blood money is due in mistaken injury, and in one of them half the blood money. For each finger of the toes, one-tenth of the blood money. Regarding the foot in intentionality, retaliation is required if cut from the ankle joint, or from the knee joint, or from the hip joint. But if cut from other than the joint, retaliation is not required. In al-Dhakhira: Similarly, the ruling for the toes: if cut from the joint intentionally, retaliation is necessary. If the leg is cut by mistake from mid-calf, the blood money for the foot is obligatory, and hukumat al-adl for what is beyond the foot. The discussion is analogous to the hand if cut from mid-forearm. If he breaks his thigh and it heals and becomes straight, there is nothing on him. In the view of Abu Yusuf, hukumat al-adl. Abu Sulayman narrated from Muhammad in Kitab al-Kharaj that Abu Hanifa said: Whatever from a person is broken—hand, foot, or otherwise—and heals and returns to its original state, there is no 'aql (blood money) for it. If there is a defect, such that the bone heals but there remains a swelling, then there is from its 'aql according to the amount of deficiency. Similarly, for a bodily wound if it heals and returns to its state, there is nothing for it.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage covers injuries to the lower limbs. For the feet: accidental cutting of both feet requires full diyah; one foot, half diyah. Each toe carries one-tenth of the full diyah (so ten toes = full diyah). Intentional amputation of the foot from a joint (ankle, knee, or hip) requires retaliation (qisas), but if cut from a non-joint area (e.g., mid-shin), retaliation is not applicable. The same rule applies to toes: if cut at the joint intentionally, qisas. For an accidental cut at mid-calf, the victim receives the full diyah for the foot (since the foot is lost) plus hukumat al-adl for the rest of the leg below the knee—analogous to a hand cut from mid-forearm. Regarding broken bones: Abu Hanifa holds that if a bone breaks and heals perfectly straight with no defect, no compensation is due. Abu Yusuf disagrees, requiring hukumat al-adl for the risk and pain. However, if a deformity or swelling remains, compensation is proportional to the defect. The same principle applies to any body wound that heals completely—no blood money.

Key Terms
عقل ('aql): Blood money or compensation for injury; synonymous with diyah in this context.
قصاص (qisas): Retributive retaliation in kind for intentional bodily harm or homicide.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone deliberately cuts another's foot from the middle of the shin (not at a joint), what is the ruling?
A) Qisas is required
B) Full diyah is due
C) Hukumat al-adl only
D) No compensation

Key Takeaway
Compensation for lower limb injuries follows fixed diyah amounts and proportionate valuation, while qisas is limited to cuts at joints; a perfectly healed fracture incurs no compensation per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Compensation for Specific Injuries: Incontinence and Loss of Function
Rulings on compensation for specific injuries causing loss of function.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the compensation (diyah) for the three specific injuries (anal stab causing fecal incontinence, blow causing urinary incontinence, and vaginal cut causing loss of penetrability) and the half-diyah rule for unilateral cut.

Core Idea
Full diyah is due for any injury causing permanent incontinence or loss of sexual function.

The text outlines three specific injuries that entail full blood money: anal stab leading to fecal incontinence, blow leading to urinary incontinence, and cutting the vagina leading to loss of penetrability. These are considered permanent losses of bodily function that warrant complete compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three injuries
Find in the passage the three distinct injuries: (1) stab in the anus causing fecal incontinence, (2) blow causing urinary incontinence, (3) cut to the vagina causing loss of penetrability.
Each is described with the consequence: 'la yastamsik' (cannot retain).
2
Note the consequence
Each injury results in a permanent loss of a bodily function: stool control, urine control, or sexual function.
3
State the ruling
For each, the ruling is 'fihi al-diyah' (full blood money is due).
This is a fixed compensation from the perpetrator or his 'aqila if unintentional.
4
Note the variant
If the vaginal cut is on one side only, half diyah is due; if bilateral, full diyah.
This is from al-Yanabi' as quoted in the text.
5
Confirm authority
These rulings are from Zahir al-Riwayah, well-established in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا طعن برمح أو غيره في دبره وصار لا يستمسك الطعام في جوفه ففيه الدية، وإذا ضرب فسلسل بوله وصار بحال لا يستمسكه ففيه الدية، وإذا ضرب فقطع فرج امرأة وصارت يحال لا يمكن جماعها ففيه الدية. وفي الينابيع : وكذا لو قطع فرجها من الجانبين حتى وصل إلى العظم، وإن قطع أحدهما ففيه نصف الدية. وفي فتاوى سمرقند : فإن جامع امرأة لا يجامع مثلها فماتت فعلى عاقلته ديتها . وفي جنايات المنتقى : إذا جامع امرأة فأفضاها حتى لا تستمسك البول فلا شيء عليه وهذا قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : إن كانت لا تستمسك البول فعليه الدية في ماله، وإن كانت تستمسك فعليه ثلث الدية وفي الكبرى : وإن كانت بحيث تستمسك ففيها ثلث الدية وفي فتاوى الخلاصة : رجل جامع صغيرة لا يجامع مثلها فماتت، فإن كانت أجنبية فالدية على العاقلة، وإن كانت منكوحته فالدية على العاقلة والمهر على الزوج، ولو أزال بكارة امرأة بالحجر أو غيره يجب المهر . وفي الينابيع : وإن زني بها مطاوعة وأفضاها فلا شيء عليه عندهما. وقال أبو يوسف: تجب الدية على عاقلته وفي الينابيع : وإذا ضرب امرأة فأقضاها وصارت بحيث لا تستمسك، فإن كانت بكراً يجب جميع الدية ولا يجب المهر عندهما. وقال محمد رحمه الله : يجمع بينهما. وفي التجريد وقال أبو يوسف وإذا وطئ امرأة بشبهة فأفضاها وصارت لا تستمسك البول تجب الدية ولا مهر .لها. وقال محمد لها المهر والدية . ولو دق فخذها أو يدها من الوطء فأرش ذلك في ماله لأنه قد يقع على جسدها، وفي المجامع يتعمد ذلك فهذا منه عمد. وعن أبي يوسف عن محمد: رجل جامع امرأة ومثلها يجامع فمماتت من شيء عليه. وقال أبو يوسف : إذا جامع امرأة فذهب منها عين أو أفضاها إن ماتت فهو ضامن. وقال محمد يضمن في هذا أكله إلا الإفضاء والقتل في الجماع وهو قول أبي حنيفة فيما حكي عن هشام عن محمد قال : وهو قول أبي يوسف وعن الفقيه أبي نصر الدبوسي : إذا دفع أجنبية فوقعت وذهبت عذرتها فعلى الدافع مثلها والتعزير. وعن الشيخ الإمام أبي حفص الكبير سئل عمن دفع امرأة فذهبت عذرتها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها كان عليه نصف المهر في قول أبي حنيفة وإحدى الروايتين عن أبي يوسف عليه جميع المهر. بكر دفعت بكراً أخرى فزالت عذرتها قال محمد على الدافعة مهر مثل الأخرى.
If he stabs with a spear or other in his anus and he cannot retain food in his stomach, then full blood money is due. If he strikes and he becomes incontinent of urine and in a state where he cannot retain it, then full blood money is due. If he strikes and cuts a woman's vagina and she becomes unable to be penetrated, then full blood money is due. In al-Yanabi': similarly, if he cuts her vagina from both sides until reaching the bone, and if he cuts one side, then half blood money. In Fatawa Samarqand: if he has intercourse with a woman who is not normally capable of intercourse and she dies, then her blood money is on his 'aqila. In Jinaayat al-Muntaqa: if he has intercourse with a woman and causes ifda' (rupture) such that she cannot retain urine, then nothing is on him. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: if she cannot retain urine, then blood money is due from his property; if she can retain, then one-third of blood money. In al-Kubra: if she can retain, then one-third blood money. In Fatawa al-Khulasa: a man has intercourse with a minor who is not normally penetrated and she dies; if she is a stranger, blood money on the 'aqila; if she is his wife, blood money on the 'aqila and the mahr on the husband. If he removes a woman's virginity with a stone or otherwise, the mahr is obligatory. In al-Yanabi': if he commits zina with her willingly and causes ifda', nothing is on him according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: blood money is due on his 'aqila. In al-Yanabi': if he strikes a woman and causes ifda' and she becomes unable to retain urine; if she was a virgin, full blood money is due and no mahr according to the two. Muhammad said: combine both. In al-Tajrid: Abu Yusuf said: if he has intercourse with a woman by shubha and causes ifda' and she cannot retain urine, blood money is due and no mahr for her. Muhammad said: she has mahr and blood money. If he crushes her thigh or hand from intercourse, then the compensation for that is from his property because it may fall on her body, and in the act of intercourse intentionally, this is intentional. From Abu Yusuf from Muhammad: a man who has intercourse with a woman who is normally capable and she dies, there is nothing on him. Abu Yusuf said: if he has intercourse with a woman and she loses an eye or he causes ifda' and she dies, he is liable. Muhammad said: he is liable in all of this except ifda' and killing in intercourse, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa as narrated from Hisham from Muhammad; he said: this is the saying of Abu Yusuf. From al-Faqih Abu Nasr al-Dabusi: if he pushes a stranger woman and she falls and loses her virginity, then on the pusher is her mithl and ta'zir. From al-Shaykh al-Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir: he was asked about a man who pushed a woman and she lost her virginity, then he divorced her before consummation; according to Abu Hanifa, half the mahr is due; in one narration from Abu Yusuf, full mahr is due. A virgin pushed another virgin and her virginity was lost; Muhammad said: on the pusher is the mahr mithl of the other.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a detailed fiqhi discussion on various injuries and their compensations, especially those affecting bodily functions and sexual organs. It begins with three specific injuries: (1) stabbing the anus causing fecal incontinence – full diyah; (2) causing urinary incontinence – full diyah; (3) cutting a woman's vagina causing loss of penetrability – full diyah. If the cut is on one side only, half diyah. The text then addresses injuries from sexual intercourse, with significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The key issue is ifda' (rupture of the vaginal wall causing incontinence) and death from intercourse. The positions diverge: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad generally hold that no compensation is due for ifda' from consensual intercourse (even if death occurs in the case of a woman normally capable of intercourse), while Abu Yusuf imposes diyah in some cases. The `aqila (tribal guarantors) bear the diyah for accidental death from intercourse with a woman not normally capable. For defloration (removal of hymen) by stone or similar, mahr is due. Pushing a woman causing loss of virginity requires mahr mithl and ta'zir. These rulings reflect the Hanafi approach of differentiating between direct physical force (jinayat) and incidental harm from a permissible act (intercourse), with istihsan playing a role.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money; fixed compensation for homicide or bodily injury.
إفضاء (ifda'): Rupture of the vaginal wall causing a passage between vagina and bladder/rectum, leading to incontinence.
عاقلة ('aqila): The group (tribe or relatives) responsible for paying diyah for accidental homicide or injury caused by a member.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Half diyah
B) Full diyah
C) One-third diyah
D) No compensation

Key Takeaway
Permanent loss of continence or sexual function due to injury requires full blood money.

Ifda' and Death from Sexual Intercourse: Hanafi Perspectives
Intra-Hanafi disputes on compensation for ifda' and death from intercourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Abu Yusuf) on compensation for ifda' and death from consensual intercourse, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
For consensual intercourse, ifda' does not incur diyah unless the woman is not normally capable; intentional harm from intercourse is treated as injury.

This passage delves into the complex rulings on ifda' (rupture causing incontinence) and death from sexual intercourse. The Hanafi school has significant internal differences, with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad generally exempting the man from compensation in consensual acts, while Abu Yusuf imposes diyah in certain cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key scenarios
The text discusses: (a) ifda' without death, (b) death from intercourse. Also covered: defloration and pushing causing virginity loss.
Focus first on ifda' and death.
2
State the majority view on ifda'
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: if a man has consensual intercourse with an adult woman and causes ifda', no compensation is due. This is stated in Jinaayat al-Muntaqa.
The act is permissible and harm is incidental.
3
Note Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf differs: if incontinence results, full diyah from his property; if only minor, one-third diyah.
Also, in cases of zina with willing partner, Abu Yusuf imposes diyah on 'aqila.
4
Consider death from intercourse
If a man has intercourse with a woman who is not normally capable of intercourse (e.g., minor) and she dies, diyah is on his 'aqila, regardless of marriage. If she is normally capable, the majority view is nothing, but Abu Yusuf imposes liability.
The text from Fatawa Samarqand and Fatawa al-Khulasa.
5
Distinguish other cases
Defloration by stone or similar requires mahr. Pushing causing virginity loss requires mahr mithl and ta'zir. These are separate from ifda'.
These show that intentional harm outside intercourse is compensable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا طعن برمح أو غيره في دبره وصار لا يستمسك الطعام في جوفه ففيه الدية، وإذا ضرب فسلسل بوله وصار بحال لا يستمسكه ففيه الدية، وإذا ضرب فقطع فرج امرأة وصارت يحال لا يمكن جماعها ففيه الدية. وفي الينابيع : وكذا لو قطع فرجها من الجانبين حتى وصل إلى العظم، وإن قطع أحدهما ففيه نصف الدية. وفي فتاوى سمرقند : فإن جامع امرأة لا يجامع مثلها فماتت فعلى عاقلته ديتها . وفي جنايات المنتقى : إذا جامع امرأة فأفضاها حتى لا تستمسك البول فلا شيء عليه وهذا قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : إن كانت لا تستمسك البول فعليه الدية في ماله، وإن كانت تستمسك فعليه ثلث الدية وفي الكبرى : وإن كانت بحيث تستمسك ففيها ثلث الدية وفي فتاوى الخلاصة : رجل جامع صغيرة لا يجامع مثلها فماتت، فإن كانت أجنبية فالدية على العاقلة، وإن كانت منكوحته فالدية على العاقلة والمهر على الزوج، ولو أزال بكارة امرأة بالحجر أو غيره يجب المهر . وفي الينابيع : وإن زني بها مطاوعة وأفضاها فلا شيء عليه عندهما. وقال أبو يوسف: تجب الدية على عاقلته وفي الينابيع : وإذا ضرب امرأة فأقضاها وصارت بحيث لا تستمسك، فإن كانت بكراً يجب جميع الدية ولا يجب المهر عندهما. وقال محمد رحمه الله : يجمع بينهما. وفي التجريد وقال أبو يوسف وإذا وطئ امرأة بشبهة فأفضاها وصارت لا تستمسك البول تجب الدية ولا مهر .لها. وقال محمد لها المهر والدية . ولو دق فخذها أو يدها من الوطء فأرش ذلك في ماله لأنه قد يقع على جسدها، وفي المجامع يتعمد ذلك فهذا منه عمد. وعن أبي يوسف عن محمد: رجل جامع امرأة ومثلها يجامع فمماتت من شيء عليه. وقال أبو يوسف : إذا جامع امرأة فذهب منها عين أو أفضاها إن ماتت فهو ضامن. وقال محمد يضمن في هذا أكله إلا الإفضاء والقتل في الجماع وهو قول أبي حنيفة فيما حكي عن هشام عن محمد قال : وهو قول أبي يوسف وعن الفقيه أبي نصر الدبوسي : إذا دفع أجنبية فوقعت وذهبت عذرتها فعلى الدافع مثلها والتعزير. وعن الشيخ الإمام أبي حفص الكبير سئل عمن دفع امرأة فذهبت عذرتها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها كان عليه نصف المهر في قول أبي حنيفة وإحدى الروايتين عن أبي يوسف عليه جميع المهر. بكر دفعت بكراً أخرى فزالت عذرتها قال محمد على الدافعة مهر مثل الأخرى.
If he stabs with a spear or other in his anus and he cannot retain food in his stomach, then full blood money is due. If he strikes and he becomes incontinent of urine and in a state where he cannot retain it, then full blood money is due. If he strikes and cuts a woman's vagina and she becomes unable to be penetrated, then full blood money is due. In al-Yanabi': similarly, if he cuts her vagina from both sides until reaching the bone, and if he cuts one side, then half blood money. In Fatawa Samarqand: if he has intercourse with a woman who is not normally capable of intercourse and she dies, then her blood money is on his 'aqila. In Jinaayat al-Muntaqa: if he has intercourse with a woman and causes ifda' (rupture) such that she cannot retain urine, then nothing is on him. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: if she cannot retain urine, then blood money is due from his property; if she can retain, then one-third of blood money. In al-Kubra: if she can retain, then one-third blood money. In Fatawa al-Khulasa: a man has intercourse with a minor who is not normally penetrated and she dies; if she is a stranger, blood money on the 'aqila; if she is his wife, blood money on the 'aqila and the mahr on the husband. If he removes a woman's virginity with a stone or otherwise, the mahr is obligatory. In al-Yanabi': if he commits zina with her willingly and causes ifda', nothing is on him according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: blood money is due on his 'aqila. In al-Yanabi': if he strikes a woman and causes ifda' and she becomes unable to retain urine; if she was a virgin, full blood money is due and no mahr according to the two. Muhammad said: combine both. In al-Tajrid: Abu Yusuf said: if he has intercourse with a woman by shubha and causes ifda' and she cannot retain urine, blood money is due and no mahr for her. Muhammad said: she has mahr and blood money. If he crushes her thigh or hand from intercourse, then the compensation for that is from his property because it may fall on her body, and in the act of intercourse intentionally, this is intentional. From Abu Yusuf from Muhammad: a man who has intercourse with a woman who is normally capable and she dies, there is nothing on him. Abu Yusuf said: if he has intercourse with a woman and she loses an eye or he causes ifda' and she dies, he is liable. Muhammad said: he is liable in all of this except ifda' and killing in intercourse, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa as narrated from Hisham from Muhammad; he said: this is the saying of Abu Yusuf. From al-Faqih Abu Nasr al-Dabusi: if he pushes a stranger woman and she falls and loses her virginity, then on the pusher is her mithl and ta'zir. From al-Shaykh al-Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir: he was asked about a man who pushed a woman and she lost her virginity, then he divorced her before consummation; according to Abu Hanifa, half the mahr is due; in one narration from Abu Yusuf, full mahr is due. A virgin pushed another virgin and her virginity was lost; Muhammad said: on the pusher is the mahr mithl of the other.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a detailed fiqhi discussion on various injuries and their compensations, especially those affecting bodily functions and sexual organs. It begins with three specific injuries: (1) stabbing the anus causing fecal incontinence – full diyah; (2) causing urinary incontinence – full diyah; (3) cutting a woman's vagina causing loss of penetrability – full diyah. If the cut is on one side only, half diyah. The text then addresses injuries from sexual intercourse, with significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The key issue is ifda' (rupture of the vaginal wall causing incontinence) and death from intercourse. The positions diverge: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad generally hold that no compensation is due for ifda' from consensual intercourse (even if death occurs in the case of a woman normally capable of intercourse), while Abu Yusuf imposes diyah in some cases. The `aqila (tribal guarantors) bear the diyah for accidental death from intercourse with a woman not normally capable. For defloration (removal of hymen) by stone or similar, mahr is due. Pushing a woman causing loss of virginity requires mahr mithl and ta'zir. These rulings reflect the Hanafi approach of differentiating between direct physical force (jinayat) and incidental harm from a permissible act (intercourse), with istihsan playing a role.

Key Terms
إفضاء (ifda'): Rupture of the vaginal wall causing a passage between vagina and bladder/rectum, leading to incontinence.
عاقلة ('aqila): The group (tribe or relatives) responsible for paying diyah for accidental homicide or injury caused by a member.
شبهة (shubha): A situation where sexual intercourse occurs under a mistaken belief of marriage or ownership, reducing the penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a man has consensual intercourse with an adult woman and causes ifda' (rupture leading to incontinence), what compensation is due?
A) Full diyah on his property
B) Full diyah on his 'aqila
C) Nothing
D) One-third diyah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the dominant view is that ifda' from consensual intercourse does not require compensation, but death from intercourse with a woman not normally capable does.

Combining Diya and Mahr for Ifḍāʾ from Intercourse Under Shubha
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for ifdha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Abu Hanifa on whether diya and mahr combine for ifdha from intercourse under shubha, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When intercourse under shubha causes ifdha, diya is due; mahr is disputed: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say only diya, Muhammad says both.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the compensation for a woman who suffers ifdha (separation of bladder and vagina) due to intercourse under shubha. The key question: does she receive blood-money (diya) alone, or both diya and a dower (mahr)? The text also extends the discussion to liability for death during such intercourse. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to distinguish between injury compensation and marital rights in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key scenarios
There are two: (1) ifdha from intercourse under shubha, (2) death from such intercourse.
2
State the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani
For ifdha: only diya, no mahr. For death: Abu Yusuf holds full liability; Muhammad and Abu Hanifa exclude ifdha and killing during intercourse.
The text says 'فأفضاها وصارت لا تستمسك البول تجب الدية ولا مهر لها'
3
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's alternative view
For ifdha: combine diya and mahr.
Muhammad said: 'لها المهر والدية'
4
Trace the reasoning
Why only diya? Because the act is not a valid marriage, so no mahr. Why combine? Because both bodily harm and loss of virginity are present.
The text does not elaborate further on the 'illa.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: the woman receives either diya only or diya plus mahr.
This affects the quantum of compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا أن تقطع الحشفة وخير بين الأرش والقود إن كان القاطع أشل أو ناقص الاصابع ذلك فلا تستمسك، فإن كانت بكراً يجب جميع الدية ولا يجب المهر عندهما. وقال محمد رحمه الله : يجمع بينهما. وفي التجريد وقال أو يوسف وإذا وطئ امرأة بشبهة فأفضاها وصارت لا تستمسك البول تجب الدية ولا مهر لها. وقال محمد لها المهر والدية . ولو دق فخذها أو يدها من الوطء فأرش ذلك في ماله لأنه قد يقع على جسدها، وفي المجامع يتعمد ذلك فهذا منه عمد. وعن أبي يوسف عن محمد: رجل جامع امرأة ومثلها يجامع فمماتت من شيء عليه. وقال أبو يوسف : إذا جامع امرأة فذهب منها عين أو أفضاها إن ماتت فهو ضامن. وقال محمد يضمن في هذا أكله إلا الإفضاء والقتل في الجماع وهو قول أبي حنيفة فيما حكي عن هشام عن محمد قال : وهو قول أبي يوسف وعن الفقيه أبي نصر الدبوسي : إذا دفع أجنبية فوقعت وذهبت عذرتها فعلى الدافع مثلها والتعزير. وعن الشيخ الإمام أبي حفص الكبير سئل عمن دفع امرأة فذهبت عذرتها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها كان عليه نصف المهر في قول أبي حنيفة وإحدى الروايتين عن أبي يوسف عليه جميع المهر. بكر دفعت بكراً أخرى فزالت عذرتها قال محمد على الدافعة مهر مثل الأخرى.
Unless the glans is cut off, and he is given choice between compensation and retaliation if the cutter was withered or missing fingers... that does not hold [urine]. If she was a virgin, full blood-money is obligatory and no dower is obligatory according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad ibn al-Hasan said: both are combined. In al-Tajrid it is reported that Abu Yusuf said: if a man has intercourse with a woman under shubha and causes ifdha (separation) so that she cannot hold urine, blood-money is obligatory and no dower for her. Muhammad said: she has both dower and blood-money. If he crushes her thigh or hand from intercourse, the compensation for that is from his wealth because it may fall on her body; in the case of intercourse he intends that, so it is intentional. From Abu Yusuf from Muhammad: a man had intercourse with a woman who is such that she could be intercourse with, and she died from something (i.e., from the act). Abu Yusuf said: if a man has intercourse with a woman and an eye or ifdha results from her, and she dies, he is liable. Muhammad said: he is liable in all this except ifdha and killing in intercourse, and that is the saying of Abu Hanifa as narrated from Hisham from Muhammad; he said: and that is the saying of Abu Yusuf. From al-Faqih Abu Nasr al-Dabusi: if he pushes a non-mahram woman and she falls and her virginity is lost, he must pay her mithl and tazir. From Sheikh al-Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir: he was asked about a man who pushed a woman and her virginity was lost, then he divorced her before consummation: according to Abu Hanifa half the dower is due, and in one of two narrations from Abu Yusuf, the full dower is due. If one virgin pushes another virgin and her virginity is lost, Muhammad said: the pusher must pay the mithl of the other.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents intra-Hanafi disputes on liability for injuries resulting from sexual intercourse and from pushing a woman. The main issue: when intercourse causes ifdha (a condition where she cannot control urine) or death, do diya and mahr combine? Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that only diya is due, no mahr, because the act is not a valid marriage. Muhammad al-Shaybani, in his view, combines both. This is consistent with the principle that both rights (bodily injury and marital right) may accrue. The text also discusses similar cases: if a man crushes a limb during intercourse, the compensation is from his wealth because it is intentional. For death from intercourse, Abu Yusuf holds he is liable; Muhammad restricts liability to cases other than ifdha and death during intercourse, which is also the view of Abu Hanifa. The passage then shifts to pushing a woman: the pusher must pay an equivalent dower (mahr al-mithl) and receive tazir (discretionary punishment). If the pusher later divorces her before consummation, Abu Hanifa holds half the dower is due (since the act is akin to consummation), while Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one half, one full. Finally, if one virgin pushes another and causes loss of virginity, the pusher must pay the mahr al-mithl of the victim. This shows that injury to the hymen is compensated by dower, not diya.

Key Terms
إفضاء (ifḍāʾ): Separation of the bladder and vagina due to injury, causing incontinence.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The equivalent dower paid to a woman of similar status, due when no specific dower is agreed.
شبهة (shubha): A doubtful situation that resembles a lawful act, reducing criminal liability but still requiring diya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding mahr for ifdha from intercourse under shubha?
A) Mahr is obligatory
B) Mahr is not obligatory
C) Mahr is half
D) Mahr is full

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, compensation for ifdha from intercourse under shubha includes diya; mahr is disputed among the imams.

Compensation for Loss of Virginity by Pushing and Divorce Afterward
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for loss of virginity by pushing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on compensation when a woman's virginity is lost due to being pushed, and apply the intra-Hanafi dispute on the dower amount when the pusher later divorces her before consummation.

Core Idea
Pushing a woman causing loss of virginity requires mahr al-mithl and tazir; divorce before consummation triggers half or full dower depending on the Hanafi imam.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two scenarios: (1) a man pushes a non-mahram woman and she falls, losing her virginity, and (2) if the same man then divorces her before consummation. It also covers the case of one virgin pushing another. Understanding these rulings clarifies the interface between tort (damage by pushing) and marital dower obligations in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scenario
Pushing a non-mahram woman causing loss of virginity.
2
State the ruling for the first scenario
The pusher must pay mahr al-mithl (equivalent dower) and receive tazir (discretionary punishment).
3
Identify the second scenario
If the pusher later marries and divorces her before consummation.
4
State the ikhtilaf on dower after divorce
Abu Hanifa: half mahr (since loss of virginity is akin to consummation). Abu Yusuf: two narrations: half or full.
5
Identify the third scenario
One virgin pushes another. Ruling: the pusher pays mahr al-mithl of the victim.

Equal Division of Blood Money in Joint Sulh
Ruling on equal division of blood money in joint sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing blood money when a free man and a slave jointly authorize a sulh, and explain the legal reasoning (talil) based on equal liability for qisas.

Core Idea
Equal qisas liability means equal blood money when both authorize the same sulh.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the ruling when a free man and a slave are both killers and their representatives jointly authorize a third party to compromise with the heirs for a lump sum. The key question: how is the lump sum divided between them? The Hanafi school rules that it is divided equally, using two lines of reasoning. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and its implications for joint liability in qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the act
Note that the killers are a free man and a slave. The slave's master (not the slave) authorizes the compromise. The free killer and the master both appoint the same agent to conduct the sulh.
The slave cannot act independently; the master represents him.
2
State the ruling on the lump sum
The ruling is that the total sum (1000 dirhams) is split equally (half each) between the free man and the slave. Understand that the slave's share is paid by his master.
The text says 'فالألف على الحر والعبد نصفان'.
3
Trace the first proof: substitute for qisas
The blood money (diya) in this sulh is a substitute (badal) for qisas. Since qisas is equally due from both killers (their lives are equally forfeit), the substitute must be divided equally.
Both are equally liable for the killing; qisas does not differentiate by free/slave status in liability.
4
Trace the second proof: contract attribution
The contract of sulh is made by the agent on behalf of both parties (free killer and master of slave). The obligation arises from this joint contract, so the sum is attributed equally to both.
Attribution to both equally results in equal obligation.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
This ruling is the established position of the Hanafi school (zahir al-riwayah) and is agreed upon within the madhhab. There is no disagreement mentioned.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وتنصف أن أمر الحر القاتل وسيد القاتل رجلاً بالصلح عن دمهما على ألف ففعل) معناه لو كان القاتل حراً وعبداً فأمر الحر القاتل ومولى العبد رجلاً بأن يصالح عن دمهما على ألف درهم ففعل المأمور فالألف على الحر والعبد نصفان لأنه مقابل بالقصاص وهو عليهما على السواء فيقسم بدله عليهما بالسواء، ولأن الألف وجبت بالعقد وهو مضاف إليهما فينصف موجبه وهو الألف عليهما.
He (the author) said: (And it is halved: that the free killer and the master of the killer command a man to compromise for their blood for a thousand, and he does). Its meaning: if the killer is a free man and a slave, then the free killer and the slave's master command a man to compromise for their blood for a thousand dirhams, and the commanded person does so, then the thousand is split equally between the free man and the slave, because it is in exchange for qisas, and qisas is upon them equally, so its substitute is divided equally between them. And also because the thousand became obligatory by contract, and it is attributed to both of them, so its obligation, the thousand, is halved between them.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage explains a specific scenario in the matn: if a free man and a slave jointly commit a murder, and their representatives (the free killer himself and the slave's master) authorize a third party to compromise with the heirs for a lump sum of one thousand dirhams, then that sum is divided equally between the free man and the slave. The reasoning is that the compensation is a substitute for qisas, and qisas is equally due from both killers (since both are liable for the same act). Therefore, its monetary equivalent is shared equally. Additionally, the contract of sulh is made on behalf of both, so the obligation is apportioned equally. This shows the Hanafi principle that when multiple persons are jointly liable for qisas, a compromise that covers all of them results in equal division of the payment.

Key Terms
تنصف (tunassaf): It is halved; the sum is divided equally between the parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if a free man and a slave jointly authorize a sulh for blood money for 1000 dirhams, how is it divided?
A) 600 for the free, 400 for the slave
B) 500 each
C) 700 for the free, 300 for the slave
D) The free pays all

Key Takeaway
When multiple killers jointly authorize a single sulh for blood money, the sum is divided equally because qisas is equally due from each.

12 min
Execution of Multiple Killers for One Victim and Vice Versa
Justifies the Hanafi ruling through istihsan and rebuts qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on executing multiple killers for one victim and one killer for multiple victims, explain the istihsan argument that overrides qiyas, and identify the practical difference with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Multiple killers can all be executed for one murder—istihsan overrides strict qiyas for deterrence.

When a group murders one person, can all be executed? Strict analogy (qiyas) from the Quranic verse 'a life for a life' suggests only one life can be taken. However, the Hanafi school, based on the practice of Caliph 'Umar and the principle of istihsan, rules that all conspirators can be executed. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and covers the reverse case of one killer for multiple victims, highlighting the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine the act under discussion: a group killing one person, and a single person killing multiple people. The Hanafi ruling is that qisas applies in both directions—all killers can be executed for one, and the single killer is executed for all.
Focus on the two scenarios separately but note the symmetry in reasoning.
2
Examine the qiyas argument against the ruling
Understand the strict analogy: the Quranic verse 'a life for a life' implies numerical equality. In qiyas, ten killers cannot equal one victim, nor can one killer equal ten victims. This would bar execution in multiple-killer or multiple-victim cases.
Identify the asl (one-for-one) and the far (multiple-for-one or one-for-multiple), and the illa of equality in number.
3
Analyze the istihsan argument
Examine why qiyas is overridden: the precedent of Caliph 'Umar executing seven for one, and his statement that he would execute all of San'a' if they conspired. The illa of deterrence (zajr) is stronger: groups murder by overpowering, so execution of all is needed to preserve the purpose of qisas—giving life to society.
Note that istihsan here is based on a stronger proof (a Companion's practice and public interest) that outweighs the analogy.
4
Understand the rebuttal to the qiyas
The author argues that the verse 'a life for a life' does not require numerical equality—it only prescribes that a soul be taken for a soul, not that the numbers must match. The required equivalence (tamathul) in qisas is achieved by considering each killer fully responsible, not by counting heads.
This refutation shows the verse is not absolute on number; other evidence (like the left eye not being taken for the right eye) proves that equality is established by other means.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position on one killer for multiple victims
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the killer is executed only for the first victim; for subsequent victims, the heirs must be compensated with diyah. The Hanafi response is that each killing is complete and independent, so equivalence requires execution for each victim. The practical difference is whether the killer dies once or multiple executions (in practice, the killer dies once, but the Hanafi ruling ensures the right of all heirs is satisfied).
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Shafi'i, some heirs may receive only blood money; under Hanafi, all can demand execution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ويقتل الجمع بالمفرد) لما روي أن سبعة من أهل صنعاء قتلوا واحداً فقتلهم عمر به وقال : لو تمالاً عليه أهل صنعاء لقتلتهم. ولأن القتل بطريق التغالب والقصاص شرع حكمه للزجر فيجعل كل واحد منهم كالمنفرد به فيجري القصاص عليهم جميعاً تحقيقاً لمعنى الإحياء، ولولا ذلك لسد باب القصاص وفتح باب التغالب إذ لا يوجد القتل من واحد غالباً لأنه يقاومه الواحد فلم يقدر عليه فلم يحصل إلا نادراً والنادر يشرع فيما يغلب لا فيما يندر . قال صاحب النهاية : هذا جواب الاستحسان. وفي القياس لا يلزمهم القصاص لأن المعتبر في القصاص المساواة لما في الزيادة من الظلم على المتعدي وفي النقصان من النجس بحق المتعدي عليه ولا مساواة بين العشرة والواحد في شيء هذا يعلم ببداهة العقل فالواحد من العشرة يكون مثلاً للواحد فكيف تكون العشرة مثلاً للواحد؟ وأيد هذا القياس قوله تعالى وكتبنا عليهم فيها أن النفس بالنفس ﴾ [المائدة : ٤٥] وذلك ينفي مقابلة النفوس بنفس ولكن ترك هذا القياس بما روي أن سبعة من أهل صنعاء قتلوا رجلاً فقضى عمر رضي الله عنه بالقصاص عليهم وقال : لو تمالاً عليه أهل صنعاء لقتلتهم به انتهى كلامه. أقول : فيه بحث لأنه بأن هذا القياس مقيد بقوله تعالى وكتبنا عليهم فيها أن النفس بالنفس ﴾ [المائدة: ٤٥] وقال في بيانه : وذلك ينفي مقابلة النفوس بنفس فعلى ذلك يلزم من ترك هذا القياس ترك العمل بمدلول الآية المذكورة وذا لا يجوز بما روي عن عمر رضي الله عنه لأن عمر إن كان منفرداً في قضائه صرح والفرد بالجمع اكتفاء فإن حضر واحد قتل وسقط حق البقية ولا يقطع يد رجلين بيد فضلاً. أحد وقوله المزبورين فظاهر لأن قول صحابي واحد وفعله لا يصلحان للمعارضة لكتاب الله تعالى الرجحان عليه وإن انضم إليه إجماع الصحابة حيث كانوا متوافرين ولم ينكر عليه عن منهم فحل محل الإجماع كما صرح به في العناية وغيرها فكذلك إذ قد تقرر في أصول الفقه أن الإجماع لا يكون ناسخاً للكتاب ولا السنة كما لا يكون القياس ناسخاً لشيء منهما، فالحق في أسلوب تحرير هذا المقام أن لا يتعرض لحديث كون الآية المذكورة مؤيدة لما هو مقتضى القياس في هذه المسألة وأن يبين عدم المنافاة بين مدلول تلك الآية وبين جواب الاستحسان ههنا وسيجيء منا الكلام في التوفيق بينهما بعيد القول إن شاء الله تعالى . قالوا : القتل بطريق التغالب غالب والقصاص شرع لحكمه الزجر فيجب تحقيقاً لحكمه الإحياء. قال صاحب العناية : لقائل أن يقول ما ذكرت من المقتول إن لم يكن قياساً على مجمع عليه لا يكون معتبراً في الشرع، وإن كان فلا يربو عن القياس المقتضى لعدمه المؤيد بقوله تعالى أن النفس بالنفس . والجواب أنه قياس سائر أبواب العقوبات المرتبة على ما يوجب الفساد من أفعال العباد ويربو على ذلك بقوة الباطن وهو إحياء كلمة الإحياء وقوله تعالى أن النفس بالنفس لا ينافيه لأنهم في إزهاق الروح الغير المتجزئ عن مجموعهم وجعلهم كشخص واحد . اهـ كلامه أقول : فيه نظر لأن جعل الأشخاص المتعددة الذوات في الحقيقة شخصاً واحداً بمجرد صدور إزهاق الروح الغير المتجزيء من مجموعهم وجعلهم متساوين كشخص واحد بحيث يتحقق بين ذلك الشخص الواحد وبين ؤلاء الجماعة مماثلة معتبرة في القصاص بعيد جداً عن مساعدة العقل والنقل، وأيضاً ينافي هذا ما سيأتي في تعليل المسألة الآتية من أن الأصل أن كل واحد منهم قاتل بوصف الكمال الصادر منهم بهذا الاعتبار فثلاث متعددة على عدد رؤوسهم فحصلت المماثلة المعتبرة في القصاص والحق عندي ههنا أن يقال : إن قوله تعالى أن النفس بالنفس لا ينافي ما قالوا في هذه المسألة إذ لا دلالة فيه على اعتبار الوحدة في النفس بل فيه مجرد مقابلة جنس النفس بجنس النفس كما ترى والمقصود منه الاحتراز عن أن تقتل النفس بما في قوله تعالى والعين بالعين والأنف بالأنف [المائدة : ٤٥] .ونحوهما وأما أنه هل تحقق المماثلة المعتبرة في القصاص عند تعذر النفس في جانب القاتل والمقتول وإنما يستفاد ذلك من دليل آخر ألا ترى أن العين اليمنى لا تقتص بالعين اليسرى وكذا العكس مع أن قوله تعالى والعين بالعين لا يدل عليه نظراً إلى ظاهر إطلاقه بل إنما يستفاد ذلك من دليل آخر فكذا هنا تبصر . قال رحمه الله : والفرد بالجمع اكتفاء) يعني إذا قتل واحد جماعة يقتل بهم يعني إذا حضر الأولياء وطلبوا وقال الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى : يقتل بالأول فقط . ولنا أنه لو قتل كل واحد بهم . منهم بوصف الكمال فيقتل بهم الحصول التماثل.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And a group is executed for one) based on the narration that seven people from San'a' killed one, so 'Umar executed them for him and said: 'If the people of San'a' had all conspired against him, I would have executed them all.' And because killing usually occurs through overpowering, and qisas is legislated for the purpose of deterrence, so each one of them is treated as if he alone killed, thus qisas applies to all of them to achieve the meaning of giving life. Without that, the door of qisas would be closed and the door of overpowering would be opened, since killing by one alone is rare because one can resist another, so it only rarely occurs, and what is rare is not legislated for what is common. The author of al-Nihaya said: 'This is the answer of istihsan.' In qiyas, qisas would not be required because what matters in qisas is equality, since any excess is injustice to the aggressor and any deficiency is injustice to the victim, and there is no equality between ten and one in anything; this is known by basic reason: one out of ten is equal to one, so how can ten be equal to one? This qiyas is supported by Allah's saying: 'And We prescribed for them therein that a life for a life' [al-Ma'idah 5:45], which negates multiple lives for one life. But this qiyas was abandoned due to the reported incident that seven people from San'a' killed a man, and 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) ordered qisas against them and said: 'If the people of San'a' had all conspired, I would have executed them all for him.' End of his words. I say: There is discussion in this because this qiyas is restricted by the verse 'a life for a life', and this negates multiple lives for one life. Consequently, abandoning this qiyas entails abandoning the implication of the mentioned verse, which is not permissible based on what is reported from 'Umar, because if 'Umar was alone in his ruling, and the individual with the group is sufficient—if one heir is present, the killer is executed and the right of the rest falls; nor is the hand of two men cut off for one hand, let alone more. And the statement of the aforementioned is apparent because the saying and action of a single Companion cannot oppose the Book of Allah, which has preponderance. Even if consensus of the Companions is added, since they were many and no one objected, it takes the place of consensus, as stated in al-'Inaya and elsewhere. Indeed, it is established in usul al-fiqh that consensus cannot abrogate the Book or the Sunnah, just as qiyas cannot abrogate either. Thus the correct approach in treating this matter is not to assert that the verse supports the qiyas in this issue, but to show that there is no contradiction between the implication of that verse and the answer of istihsan here, and later we will discuss the reconciliation, Allah willing. They said: Killing by overpowering is common, and qisas is legislated for its deterrent effect, so it must be implemented to achieve the purpose of giving life. The author of al-'Inaya said: One could say that what you mentioned about the victim, if it is not qiyas upon something agreed upon, it is not considered in the law; if it is, then it does not outweigh the qiyas that requires non-execution, supported by the verse 'a life for a life'. The answer is that this is qiyas from other chapters of penalties that correspond to corrupt actions, and it outweighs due to the inner strength, which is the word of giving life, and the verse does not contradict it because they are in causing the undivided soul to depart from their totality, and they are treated as one person. End of his words. I say: This is questionable because treating multiple individuals as one person merely because of the undivided soul's departure from their totality, and making them equal to one person such that there is equivalence in qisas, is far from supporting reason and transmitted evidence. Also this contradicts what will come in the explanation of the next issue: that the principle is that each one of them is a killer in the complete sense, so there is multiplicity according to their number, and thus equivalence in qisas is achieved. The correct view here is to say that the verse 'a life for a life' does not contradict what they said in this issue, because it does not indicate the unity of the soul; rather it merely contrasts the genus of soul with the genus of soul, and its purpose is to prevent killing a soul in exchange for something else, as in the verse 'an eye for an eye, a nose for a nose'. Whether the required equivalence in qisas is achieved when the soul is absent from the side of the killer and the victim is determined from another evidence. Do you not see that the right eye is not retaliated with the left eye, and vice versa, even though the verse 'an eye for an eye' does not indicate that based on its apparent generality? Rather it is derived from other evidence. So here too, reflect. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And the individual is executed for the group by way of sufficiency) meaning if one person kills a group, he is executed for them, i.e., if the heirs are present and demand. And Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: He is executed only for the first. Our argument is that he killed each one of them in the complete sense, so he is executed for them to achieve equivalence.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that multiple killers can all be executed for murdering a single victim, and conversely, a single killer can be executed for multiple victims. The main proof is the action of Caliph 'Umar (رضي الله عنه) who executed seven men for killing one, stating he would execute even more if they all conspired. The author explains that this is based on istihsan (juristic preference) because strict qiyas (analogy) based on the Quranic verse 'a life for a life' would suggest only one life can be taken for one. However, qiyas is overridden here by the need for deterrence (zajr) and the fact that group murder is common. The passage includes a detailed debate from various commentators (al-Nihaya, al-'Inaya) about the conflict between the verse and the ruling, and the author (from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) offers his own resolution: the verse does not require one-for-one in terms of numbers; it only requires that the soul taken is for the soul lost, not for a limb. The equivalence needed for qisas is established by considering each killer as a complete cause of death. The passage also notes the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that if one kills many, he is executed only for the first victim. The Hanafi response is that the killer is fully responsible for each death, so execution for all is justified.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides strict analogy in favor of a stronger proof or public interest.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an original case to a new case based on shared effective cause.
تماثل (tamathul): Equivalence required for qisas, i.e., the killer and victim must be matched in legal capacity and act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the Hanafi ruling that a group of killers can all be executed for murdering one person?
A) Strict analogy from the Quranic verse 'a life for a life'.
B) The practice of Caliph 'Umar and the principle of deterrence (istihsan).
C) Consensus of all Companions.
D) The hadith that 'the blood of a Muslim is not shed for a non-Muslim'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows execution of multiple killers for one victim and one killer for multiple victims, based on istihsan and the deterrent purpose of qisas, overriding the strict numerical reading of 'a life for a life'.
